\DoxyCodeLine{678         \textcolor{comment}{// Construct the accelerometer biases for push to the hardware accelerometer bias registers. These registers contain}}
\DoxyCodeLine{679         \textcolor{comment}{// factory trim values which must be added to the calculated accelerometer biases; on boot up these registers will hold}}
\DoxyCodeLine{680         \textcolor{comment}{// non-\/zero values. In addition, bit 0 of the lower byte must be preserved since it is used for temperature}}
\DoxyCodeLine{681         \textcolor{comment}{// compensation calculations. Accelerometer bias registers expect bias input as 2048 LSB per g, so that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{682         \textcolor{comment}{// the accelerometer biases calculated above must be divided by 8.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{683 }
\DoxyCodeLine{684         \textcolor{comment}{// int32\_t accel\_bias\_reg[3] = \{0, 0, 0\}; // A place to hold the factory accelerometer trim biases}}

\DoxyCodeLine{689         \textcolor{comment}{// readBytes(MPU9250\_ADDRESS, ZA\_OFFSET\_H, 2, \&data[0]);}}
\DoxyCodeLine{690         \textcolor{comment}{// accel\_bias\_reg[2] = (int32\_t) (((int16\_t)data[0] << 8) | data[1]);}}
\DoxyCodeLine{691 }
\DoxyCodeLine{692         \textcolor{comment}{// uint32\_t mask = 1uL; // Define mask for temperature compensation bit 0 of lower byte of accelerometer bias registers}}
\DoxyCodeLine{693         \textcolor{comment}{// uint8\_t mask\_bit[3] = \{0, 0, 0\}; // Define array to hold mask bit for each accelerometer bias axis}}
\DoxyCodeLine{694 }
\DoxyCodeLine{695         \textcolor{comment}{// for(ii = 0; ii < 3; ii++) \{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{696         \textcolor{comment}{//     if((accel\_bias\_reg[ii] \& mask)) mask\_bit[ii] = 0x01; // If temperature compensation bit is set, record that fact in mask\_bit}}

\DoxyCodeLine{534         \textcolor{comment}{// minimum delay time for this setting is 5.9 ms, which means sensor fusion update rates cannot}}
\DoxyCodeLine{535         \textcolor{comment}{// be higher than 1 / 0.0059 = 170 Hz}}
\DoxyCodeLine{536         \textcolor{comment}{// DLPF\_CFG = bits 2:0 = 011; this limits the sample rate to 1000 Hz for both}}
\DoxyCodeLine{537         \textcolor{comment}{// With the MPU9250, it is possible to get gyro sample rates of 32 kHz (!), 8 kHz, or 1 kHz}}
\DoxyCodeLine{538         \mbox{\hyperlink{class_m_p_u9250___a14f995d9f397191a1bc656e49cb0d294}{writeByte}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{class_m_p_u9250___af43bb93a521ad660dda737b3b39f14fd}{MPU9250\_ADDRESS}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{_m_p_u9250_register_map_8h_ab29423dbcb7f083aabb6e0aa72a5531a}{MPU\_CONFIG}}, 0x03);}
\DoxyCodeLine{539 }
\DoxyCodeLine{540         \textcolor{comment}{// Set sample rate = gyroscope output rate/(1 + SMPLRT\_DIV)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{541         \mbox{\hyperlink{class_m_p_u9250___a14f995d9f397191a1bc656e49cb0d294}{writeByte}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{class_m_p_u9250___af43bb93a521ad660dda737b3b39f14fd}{MPU9250\_ADDRESS}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{_m_p_u9250_register_map_8h_a7119c37e38b6736096ea1565459043ba}{SMPLRT\_DIV}}, 0x04);  \textcolor{comment}{// Use a 200 Hz rate; a rate consistent with the filter update rate}}

\DoxyCodeLine{543 }

\DoxyCodeLine{545         \textcolor{comment}{// Range selects FS\_SEL and GFS\_SEL are 0 -\/ 3, so 2-\/bit values are left-\/shifted into positions 4:3}}

\DoxyCodeLine{138         \textcolor{comment}{// Accel and Gyro direction is Right-\/Hand, X-\/Forward, Z-\/Up}}
\DoxyCodeLine{139         \textcolor{comment}{// Magneto direction is Right-\/Hand, Y-\/Forward, Z-\/Down}}

\DoxyCodeLine{155         \textcolor{keywordflow}{else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{156         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{157             \textcolor{comment}{// Define output variables from updated quaternion-\/-\/-\/these are Tait-\/Bryan angles, commonly used in aircraft orientation.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{158             \textcolor{comment}{// In this coordinate system, the positive z-\/axis is down toward Earth.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{159             \textcolor{comment}{// Yaw is the angle between Sensor x-\/axis and Earth magnetic North (or true North if corrected for local declination, looking down on the sensor positive yaw is counterclockwise.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{160             \textcolor{comment}{// Pitch is angle between sensor x-\/axis and Earth ground plane, toward the Earth is positive, up toward the sky is negative.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{161             \textcolor{comment}{// Roll is angle between sensor y-\/axis and Earth ground plane, y-\/axis up is positive roll.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{162             \textcolor{comment}{// These arise from the definition of the homogeneous rotation matrix constructed from quaternions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{163             \textcolor{comment}{// Tait-\/Bryan angles as well as Euler angles are non-\/commutative; that is, the get the correct orientation the rotations must be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{164             \textcolor{comment}{// applied in the correct order which for this configuration is yaw, pitch, and then roll.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{165             \textcolor{comment}{// For more see http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conversion\_between\_quaternions\_and\_Euler\_angles which has additional links.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{166             \mbox{\hyperlink{class_m_p_u9250___a9ba268b2e001d3e4f35e3eeb0b18ccee}{updateRPY}}();}
\DoxyCodeLine{167         \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{168 }
\DoxyCodeLine{169         \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} \textcolor{keyword}{true};}
\DoxyCodeLine{170     \}}
